<dt id="artificial_selection" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Selective breeding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selective_breeding">artificial selection</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called&nbsp;<strong>selective breeding</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">The process by which humans use&nbsp;<a title="Animal breeding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_breeding">animal breeding</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Plant breeding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant_breeding">plant breeding</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#natural_selection"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;natural selection">selectively</span></a>&nbsp;control the development of particular&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#phenotype"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;phenotype">phenotypic</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#phenotypic_trait"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;phenotypic trait">traits</span></a>&nbsp;in organisms by choosing which individual organisms will&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;reproduction">reproduce</span></a>&nbsp;and create&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>. While the deliberate exploitation of knowledge about&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#genetics"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;genetics">genetics</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#reproductive_biology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;reproductive biology">reproductive biology</span></a>&nbsp;in the hope of producing desirable characteristics is widely practiced in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#agriculture"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;agriculture">agriculture</span></a>&nbsp;and experimental biology, artificial selection may also be unintentional and may produce unintended (desirable or undesirable) results.</dd>
<dt id="asexual_reproduction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Asexual reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asexual_reproduction">asexual reproduction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;reproduction">reproduction</span></a>&nbsp;involving a single parent that results in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>&nbsp;that are genetically identical to the parent.</dd>
<dt id="astrobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Astrobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrobiology">astrobiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology concerned with the effects of outer space on living organisms and the search for extraterrestrial life.</dd>
<dt id="autoimmunity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Autoimmunity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autoimmunity">autoimmunity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The system of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#immunity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;immunity">immune</span></a>&nbsp;responses of an organism directed against its own healthy cells and tissues.</dd>
<dt id="autotroph" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Autotroph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autotroph">autotroph</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Sometimes used interchangeably with&nbsp;<strong><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#primary_producer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;primary producer">primary producer</span></a></strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">An organism capable of producing complex&nbsp;<a title="Organic compound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_compound">organic compounds</a>&nbsp;from simple substances present in its surroundings, generally by using energy from sunlight (as in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#photosynthesis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;photosynthesis">photosynthesis</span></a>) or from inorganic chemical reactions (as in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#chemosynthesis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;chemosynthesis">chemosynthesis</span></a>). Autotrophs do not need to consume another living organism in order to obtain energy or organic carbon, as opposed to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#heterotroph"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;heterotroph">heterotrophs</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="B" class="mw-headline">B</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="b_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="B cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B_cell">B cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of lymphocyte in the humoral immunity of the adaptive immune system.</dd>
<dt id="bacteria" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bacteria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria">bacteria</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An enormous and diverse clade of microscopic,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#prokaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;prokaryote">prokaryotic</span></a>, single-celled organisms which lack a true&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleus">nucleus</span></a>. They represent one of the three fundamental biological&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#domain"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;domain">domains</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="bacteriophage" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bacteriophage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteriophage">bacteriophage</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#virus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;virus">virus</span></a>&nbsp;that infects and multiplies within&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#bacteria"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;bacteria">bacteria</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="barr_body" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Barr body" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barr_body">Barr body</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The inactive X chromosome in a female somatic cell, rendered inactive in a process called lyonization, in those species in which sex is determined by the presence of the Y (including humans) or W chromosome rather than the diploidy of the X or Z.</dd>
<dt id="basal_body" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Basal body" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basal_body">basal body</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organelle formed from a&nbsp;<a title="Centriole" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centriole">centriole</a>, and a short cylindrical array of microtubules. Also called a&nbsp;<em>basal granule</em>, a&nbsp;<em>kinetosome</em>, and in older cytological literature, a&nbsp;<em>blepharoplast</em>.</dd>
<dt id="behavioral_ecology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Behavioral ecology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_ecology">behavioral ecology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the evolutionary basis for animal behavior due to ecological pressures.</dd>
<dt id="bile" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bile">bile</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A dark green to yellowish-brown fluid, produced by the liver of most vertebrates, which aids the digestion of&nbsp;<a title="Lipid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipid">lipids</a>&nbsp;in the small intestine. Also called&nbsp;<em>gall</em>.</dd>
<dt id="binary_fission" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Fission (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fission_(biology)">binary fission</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process by which one prokaryotic cell divides into two identical daughter cells.</dd>
<dt id="binomial_nomenclature" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Binomial nomenclature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature">binomial nomenclature</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A formal system of classifying&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>&nbsp;of living things by giving each a name composed of two parts, both of which use Latin grammatical forms, although they can be based on words from other languages.</dd>
<dt id="biocatalysis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biocatalysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biocatalysis">biocatalysis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of&nbsp;<a title="Catalysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalysis">catalysis</a>&nbsp;in biological systems. In biocatalytic processes, natural catalysts, such as protein enzymes, perform chemical transformations on organic compounds.</dd>
<dt id="biochemistry" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biochemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biochemistry">biochemistry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the chemical properties, compositions, reactions, and processes related to living organisms.</dd>
<dt id="biodiversity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biodiversity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity">biodiversity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A contraction of "biological diversity" generally referring to the variety and variability of life on Earth.</dd>
<dt id="bioengineering" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Bioengineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioengineering">bioengineering</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The application of concepts and methods of biology to solve real-world problems related to the life sciences or the application thereof.</dd>
<dt id="bioenergetics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bioenergetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioenergetics">bioenergetics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the transformation of energy in living organisms.</dd>
<dt id="biogeography" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biogeography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeography">biogeography</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the distribution of species and ecosystems in geographic space and through geological time. Organisms and biological communities often vary in a regular fashion along geographic gradients of latitude, elevation, isolation and habitat area.</dd>
<dt id="bioinformatics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Bioinformatics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The application of computer technology to the management of biological information.</dd>
<dt id="biological_organization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological organization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_organization">biological organization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The hierarchy of complex biological structures and systems, designed to define life through a reductionist approach.</dd>
<dt id="biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology">biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of life and living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organism">organisms</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="biomass" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biomass" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass">biomass</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Organic matter derived from living or recently living organisms. Biomass can be used as a source of energy and it most often refers to plants or plant-based materials which are not used for food or feed, and are specifically called lignocellulosic biomass.</dd>
<dt id="biomathematics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Biomathematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomathematics">biomathematics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The theoretical use of mathematical models and abstractions of living systems to understand and predict biological problems.</dd>
<dt id="biome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biome">biome</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any very large&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#ecology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;ecology">ecological</span></a>&nbsp;area on the Earth's surface containing fauna and flora (animals and plants) adapting to their environment. Biomes are often defined by&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#abiotic_component"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;abiotic component">abiotic factors</span></a>&nbsp;such as climate, topographical relief, geology, soils, and water resources.</dd>
<dt id="biomechanics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biomechanics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomechanics">biomechanics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the structure and function of biological systems by means of the methods of "mechanics", which is the branch of physics involving analysis of the actions of forces.</dd>
<dt id="biomedical_engineering" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biomedical engineering" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomedical_engineering">biomedical engineering</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The application of engineering principles and design concepts to medicine and biology for healthcare purposes (e.g. diagnostic or therapeutic).</dd>
<dt id="biomedical_research" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Biomedical research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomedical_research">biomedical research</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The pursuit of answers to medical questions. These investigations lead to discoveries, which in turn lead to the development of new preventions, therapies, and cures for problems in human and veterinary health. Biomedical research generally takes two forms: basic science and applied research.</dd>
<dt id="biomolecule" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biomolecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomolecule">biomolecule</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Molecules" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecules">Molecules</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ions">ions</a>&nbsp;that are present in organisms, essential to some typically biological process such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_division"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell division">cell division</span></a>,&nbsp;<a title="Morphogenesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphogenesis">morphogenesis</a>, or development.</dd>
<dt id="biophysics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biophysics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biophysics">biophysics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The application of approaches traditionally employed in physics to study biological systems.</dd>
<dt id="biotechnology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biotechnology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biotechnology">biotechnology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Biotechnology is the use of living systems and organisms to develop or make products, or "any technological application that uses biological systems, living organisms or derivatives thereof, to make or modify products or processes for specific use" (UN Convention on Biological Diversity).</dd>
<dt id="bipedal" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Bipedal" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipedal">bipedal</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A form of terrestrial locomotion where an organism moves by means of its two rear limbs or legs.</dd>
<dt id="birth" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Birth" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birth">birth</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="blastocyst" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Blastocyst" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastocyst">blastocyst</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mammalian&nbsp;<a title="Blastula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastula">blastula</a>&nbsp;in which some differentiation of cells has occurred.</dd>
<dt id="blood" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Blood" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood">blood</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Body fluid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_fluid">body fluid</a>&nbsp;that circulates in humans and other vertebrate animals and is generally responsible for delivering necessary substances such as&nbsp;<a title="Oxygen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen">oxygen</a>&nbsp;and nutrients between the cells and tissues of the body and transporting&nbsp;<a title="Metabolic waste" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metabolic_waste">metabolic waste</a>&nbsp;products away from those same cells and tissues.</dd>
<dt id="blood-brain_barrier" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Blood-brain barrier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood-brain_barrier">blood-brain barrier</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A semipermeable membrane separating the blood from the cerebrospinal fluid, and constituting a barrier to the passage of cells, particles, and large molecules.</dd>
<dt id="botany" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Botany" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Botany">botany</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#plant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;plant">plants</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="building_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Building biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Building_biology">building biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A science that leads to natural healthy ecological homes, schools, and workplaces that exist in harmony with the environment.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="C" class="mw-headline">C</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="calvin_cycle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Light-independent reactions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-independent_reactions#Coupling_to_other_metabolic_pathways">Calvin cycle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The Calvin cycle, light-independent reactions, bio synthetic phase, dark reactions, or photosynthetic carbon reduction (PCR) cycle&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Photosynthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>&nbsp;are the chemical reactions that convert carbon dioxide and other compounds into&nbsp;<a title="Glucose" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glucose">glucose</a>. These reactions occur in the&nbsp;<a title="Stroma (fluid)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroma_(fluid)">stroma</a>, the fluid-filled area of a&nbsp;<a title="Chloroplast" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloroplast">chloroplast</a>&nbsp;outside the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Thylakoid membranes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thylakoid_membranes">thylakoid membranes</a>. These reactions take the products (<a title="Adenosine triphosphate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate">ATP</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="NADPH" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NADPH">NADPH</a>) of&nbsp;<a title="Light-dependent reactions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-dependent_reactions">light-dependent reactions</a>&nbsp;and perform further chemical processes on them. There are three phases to the light-independent reactions, collectively called the&nbsp;<em>Calvin cycle</em>: carbon fixation, reduction reactions, and ribulose 1,5-bisphosphate (RuBP) regeneration.</dd>
<dt id="carbon_fixation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Carbon fixation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_fixation">carbon fixation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The conversion process of inorganic carbon (carbon dioxide) to organic compounds by living organisms.</dd>
<dt id="carbonate" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Carbonate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbonate">carbonate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any member of two classes of chemical compounds derived from carbonic acid or carbon dioxide.</dd>
<dt id="carotenoid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Carotenoid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carotenoid">carotenoid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of a class of organic pigments produced by&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#algae"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;algae">algae</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#plant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;plant">plants</span></a>, as well as certain&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#bacteria"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;bacteria">bacteria</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fungi"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fungi">fungi</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="catalase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Catalase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalase">catalase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#enzyme"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;enzyme">enzyme</span></a>&nbsp;found in nearly all living&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Organisms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisms">organisms</a>&nbsp;exposed to&nbsp;<a title="Oxygen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen">oxygen</a>, including bacteria, plants, and animals.</dd>
<dt id="cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_(biology)">cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The basic structural and functional unit of all living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organism">organisms</span></a>, and the smallest functional unit of life. A cell may exist as an independent, self-replicating unit (as in the case of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#unicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;unicellular">unicellular organisms</span></a>), or in cooperation with other cells, each of which may be specialized for carrying out particular functions within a larger&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#multicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;multicellular">multicellular organism</span></a>. Cells consist of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytoplasm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytoplasm">cytoplasm</span></a>&nbsp;enclosed within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">cell membrane</span></a>&nbsp;and sometimes a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_wall"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell wall">cell wall</span></a>, and serve the fundamental purpose of separating the controlled environment in which biochemical processes take place from the outside world. Most cells are visible only under a&nbsp;<a title="Microscope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microscope">microscope</a>.</dd>
<dt id="cell_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_biology">cell biology</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called&nbsp;<strong>cytology</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the structure and function of living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>, including their&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#physiology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;physiology">physiological</span></a>&nbsp;properties,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metabolism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metabolism">metabolic</span></a>&nbsp;processes, chemical composition,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#life_cycle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;life cycle">life cycle</span></a>, the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organelle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organelle">organelles</span></a>&nbsp;they contain, and their interactions with their environment. This is done at both&nbsp;<a title="Microscope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microscope">microscopic</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#molecular_biology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;molecular biology">molecular</span></a>&nbsp;levels.</dd>
<dt id="cell_cycle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_cycle">cell cycle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The ordered series of events which take place in a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>&nbsp;leading to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA_replication"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA replication">duplication</span></a>&nbsp;of its genetic material and ultimately the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_division"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell division">division</span></a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytoplasm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytoplasm">cytoplasm</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organelle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organelle">organelles</span></a>&nbsp;to produce two or more daughter cells. These events can be broadly divided into phases of growth and division, each of which can vary in duration and complexity depending on the tissue or organism to which the cell belongs. Cell cycles are essential processes in all&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#unicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;unicellular">unicellular</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#multicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;multicellular">multicellular</span></a>&nbsp;organisms.</dd>
<dt id="cell_division" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell division" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_division">cell division</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any process by which a parent&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>&nbsp;divides into two or more daughter cells. Examples include&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#binary_fission"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;binary fission">binary fission</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#mitosis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;mitosis">mitosis</span></a>, and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#meiosis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;meiosis">meiosis</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="cell_membrane" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell membrane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_membrane">cell membrane</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The semipermeable&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">membrane</span></a>&nbsp;surrounding the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytoplasm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytoplasm">cytoplasm</span></a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="cell_nucleus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell nucleus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus">cell nucleus</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The "control room" for the cell. The nucleus gives out all the orders.</dd>
<dt id="cell_plate" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell plate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_plate">cell plate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Grown in the cell's center, it fuses with the parental plasma membrane, creating a new cell wall that enables cell division.</dd>
<dt id="cell_theory" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_theory">cell theory</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The theory that all living things are made up of cells.</dd>
<dt id="cell_wall" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cell wall" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_wall">cell wall</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A tough, often rigid structural barrier surrounding certain types of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>&nbsp;(such as in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fungi"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fungi">fungi</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#plant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;plant">plants</span></a>, and most&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#prokaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;prokaryote">prokaryotes</span></a>) that is immediately external to the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">cell membrane</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="cellular" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">cellular</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of or relating to a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="central_dogma_of_molecular_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Central dogma of molecular biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_dogma_of_molecular_biology">central dogma of molecular biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A framework for understanding the movement of genetic information between information-carrying&nbsp;<a title="Biopolymer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biopolymer">biopolymers</a>&nbsp;within biological systems. Popularly (though simplistically) stated as "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;makes&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;and RNA makes&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">protein</span></a>", the principle attempts to capture the notion that the transfer of genetic information only naturally occurs between certain classes of molecules and in certain directions.</dd>
<dt id="centriole" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Centriole" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centriole">centriole</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cylindrical cell structure composed mainly of a protein called tubulin that is found in most eukaryotic cells.</dd>
<dt id="centrosome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Centrosome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrosome">centrosome</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organelle that is the main place where cell microtubules get organized, occurring only in plant and animal cells and regulating the cell division cycle.</dd>
<dt id="chemical_compound" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical compound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_compound">chemical compound</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A chemical substance consisting of two or more different&nbsp;<a title="Chemical bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_bond">chemically bonded</a>&nbsp;<a title="Chemical element" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_element">elements</a>, with a fixed ratio determining the composition. The ratio of each element is usually expressed by a&nbsp;<a title="Chemical formula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_formula">chemical formula</a>.</dd>
<dt id="chemical_equilibrium" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical equilibrium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_equilibrium">chemical equilibrium</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The state in which both reactants and products are present in concentrations which have no further tendency to change with time in a chemical reaction.</dd>
<dt id="chemical_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemical reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_reaction">chemical reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A process that leads to the transformation of one set of chemical substances to another.</dd>
<dt id="chemistry" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry">chemistry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A branch of the physical sciences that studies the composition, structure, properties, and change of&nbsp;<a title="Matter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matter">matter</a>. Chemical interactions underlie all biological processes.</dd>
<dt id="chemosynthesis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chemosynthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemosynthesis">chemosynthesis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="chlorophyll" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chlorophyll" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any of several&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#photosynthesis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;photosynthesis">photosynthetic</span></a>&nbsp;pigments found in&nbsp;<a title="Cyanobacteria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanobacteria">cyanobacteria</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Algae" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae">algae</a>, or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#plant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;plant">plants</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="chloroplast" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chloroplast" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloroplast">chloroplast</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Organelles, specialized subunits, in plant and algal cells, main role of which is to conduct photosynthesis, where the photosynthetic pigment chlorophyll captures the energy from sunlight and converts and stores it in the energy-storage molecules ATP and NADPH while freeing oxygen from water.</dd>
<dt id="cholesterol" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cholesterol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cholesterol">cholesterol</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organic molecule, a sterol, a type of lipid molecule, and biosynthesized by all animal cells because it is an essential structural component of all animal cell membranes&mdash;essential to maintain both membrane structural integrity and fluidity.</dd>
<dt id="chromosome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Chromosome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome">chromosome</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A threadlike strand of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Cell nucleus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus">cell nucleus</a>&nbsp;that carries the&nbsp;<a title="Gene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene">genes</a>&nbsp;in a linear order.</dd>
<dt id="cilia" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Cilia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cilia">cilia</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="circadian_rhythm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Circadian rhythm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circadian_rhythm">circadian rhythm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="citric_acid_cycle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Citric acid cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citric_acid_cycle">citric acid cycle</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called the&nbsp;<strong>Krebs cycle</strong>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<strong>tricarboxylic acid cycle (TCA)</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A series of chemical reactions used by all aerobic organisms to generate energy through the oxidation of acetyl-CoA derived from carbohydrates, fats and proteins into carbon dioxide and chemical energy in the form of guanosine triphosphate (GTP). In addition, the cycle provides precursors of certain amino acids as well as the reducing agent NADH that is used in numerous other biochemical reactions. Its central importance to many biochemical pathways suggests that it was one of the earliest established components of cellular metabolism and may have originated abiogenically.</dd>
<dt id="clade" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Clade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clade">clade</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="class" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Class (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(biology)">class</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="clonal_selection" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Clonal selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clonal_selection">clonal selection</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Clonal selection theory is a&nbsp;<a title="Scientific theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_theory">scientific theory</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Immunology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunology">immunology</a>&nbsp;that explains the functions of cells (<a class="mw-redirect" title="Lymphocytes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lymphocytes">lymphocytes</a>) of the&nbsp;<a title="Immune system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immune_system">immune system</a>&nbsp;in response to specific&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antigens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigens">antigens</a>&nbsp;invading the body. The theory has become the widely accepted model for how the&nbsp;<a title="Immune system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immune_system">immune system</a>&nbsp;responds to&nbsp;<a title="Infection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infection">infection</a>&nbsp;and how certain types of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="B cells" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B_cells">B</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="T lymphocytes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T_lymphocytes">T lymphocytes</a>&nbsp;are selected for destruction of specific&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Antigens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigens">antigens</a>.</dd>
<dt id="cloning" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cloning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloning">cloning</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of producing similar populations of genetically identical individuals that occurs in nature when organisms such as bacteria, insects or plants reproduce asexually.</dd>
<dt id="colony" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Colony (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_(biology)">colony</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="conservation_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Conservation biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_biology">conservation biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The scientific study of nature and of Earth's biodiversity with the aim of protecting species, their habitats, and ecosystems from excessive rates of extinction and the erosion of biotic interactions.</dd>
<dt id="convergent_evolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Convergent evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convergent_evolution">convergent evolution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The independent development of similar characteristics in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>&nbsp;of different lineages.</dd>
<dt id="countercurrent_exchange" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Countercurrent exchange" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Countercurrent_exchange">countercurrent exchange</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mechanism that happens in&nbsp;<a title="Nature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature">nature</a>&nbsp;and is mimicked in industry and engineering, in which there is a crossover of some property, usually heat or some component, between two flowing bodies flowing in opposite directions to each other.</dd>
<dt id="crista" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Crista" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crista">crista</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fold in the inner&nbsp;<a title="Membrane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Membrane">membrane</a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#mitochondria"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;mitochondria">mitochondrion</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="cryobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cryobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryobiology">cryobiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the effects of low temperatures on living things within Earth's&nbsp;<a title="Cryosphere" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryosphere">cryosphere</a>&nbsp;or in laboratory experiments.</dd>
<dt id="cytology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Cytology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytology">cytology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_biology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell biology">cell biology</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="cytoplasm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cytoplasm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoplasm">cytoplasm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">All of the material within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>&nbsp;and enclosed by the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">cell membrane</span></a>, except for the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleus">nucleus</span></a>. The cytoplasm consists mainly of water, the gel-like&nbsp;<a title="Cytosol" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytosol">cytosol</a>, various&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organelle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organelle">organelles</span></a>, and free-floating granules of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nutrient"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nutrient">nutrients</span></a>&nbsp;and other&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#biomolecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;biomolecule">biomolecules</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="cytosine" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cytosine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytosine">cytosine</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the four main nucleotide bases found in DNA and RNA, along with adenine, guanine, thymine, and uracil (in RNA); it is a pyrimidine derivative, with a heterocyclic aromatic ring and two substituents attached (an amine group at position 4 and a keto group at position 2).</dd>
<dt id="cytoskeleton" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Cytoskeleton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoskeleton">cytoskeleton</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cytoskeleton is present in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytoplasm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytoplasm">cytoplasm</span></a>&nbsp;of all&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>, including&nbsp;<a title="Bacteria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria">bacteria</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Archaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaea">archaea</a>. It is a complex, dynamic network of interlinking&nbsp;<a title="Protein filament" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protein_filament">protein filaments</a>&nbsp;that extends from the&nbsp;<a title="Cell nucleus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus">cell nucleus</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Cell membrane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_membrane">cell membrane</a>.&nbsp;The cytoskeletal systems of different organisms are composed of similar proteins. In eukaryotes, the cytoskeletal matrix is a dynamic structure composed of three main proteins, which are capable of rapid growth or disassembly dependent on the cell's requirements.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="D" class="mw-headline">D</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="darwinian_fitness" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Darwinian fitness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darwinian_fitness">Darwinian fitness</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The genetic contribution of an individual to the next generation's gene pool relative to the average for the population, usually measured by the number of offspring or close kin that survive to reproductive age.</dd>
<dt id="deciduous" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Deciduous" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deciduous">deciduous</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Deciduous means "falling off at maturity" or "tending to fall off", and it is typically used in order to refer to trees or shrubs that lose their leaves seasonally (most commonly during autumn) and to the shedding of other plant structures such as petals after flowering or fruit when ripe.</dd>
<dt id="decomposition" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Decomposition" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decomposition">decomposition</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="dehydration_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dehydration reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dehydration_reaction">dehydration reaction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A chemical reaction that involves the loss of a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Water molecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_molecule">water molecule</a>&nbsp;from the reacting molecule.</dd>
<dt id="denaturation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Denaturation (biochemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denaturation_(biochemistry)">denaturation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A process in which proteins or nucleic acids lose the quaternary, tertiary and secondary structure which is present in their native state, by application of some external stress or compound such as a strong acid or base, a concentrated inorganic salt, or an organic solvent.</dd>
<dt id="dendrite" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dendrite" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dendrite">dendrite</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short branched extension of a nerve cell, along which impulses received from other cells at synapses are transmitted to the cell body.</dd>
<dt id="denitrification" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Denitrification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denitrification">denitrification</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A microbially facilitated process of nitrate reduction (performed by a large group of heterotrophic facultative anaerobic bacteria) that may ultimately produce molecular nitrogen (N<sub>2</sub>) through a series of intermediate gaseous&nbsp;<a title="Nitrogen oxide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide">nitrogen oxide</a>&nbsp;products. Part of the&nbsp;<a title="Nitrogen cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle">nitrogen cycle</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="deoxyribonucleic_acid_(dna)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Deoxyribonucleic acid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deoxyribonucleic_acid">deoxyribonucleic acid</a>&nbsp;(DNA)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleic_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleic acid">nucleic acid</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#polymer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;polymer">polymer</span></a>&nbsp;that serves as the fundamental hereditary material in all living organisms. A set of four&nbsp;<a title="Nucleobase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleobase">bases</a>&nbsp;is used in the&nbsp;<a title="Nucleotide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotide">nucleotide</a>&nbsp;sequences which comprise each DNA molecule:&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#adenine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;adenine">adenine</span></a>&nbsp;(abbreviated A),&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytosine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytosine">cytosine</span></a>&nbsp;(C),&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#guanine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;guanine">guanine</span></a>&nbsp;(G), and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#thymine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;thymine">thymine</span></a>&nbsp;(T); these four bases are individually attached to a sugar-phosphate complex to form a complete nucleotide.</dd>
<dt id="depolarization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Depolarization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depolarization">depolarization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of reversing the charge across a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">cell membrane</span></a>&nbsp;(such as that of a&nbsp;<a title="Neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuron">neuron</a>), thereby causing an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#action_potential"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;action potential">action potential</span></a>. In depolarization, the inside of the membrane, which is normally negatively charged, becomes positive and the outside becomes negative. This is brought about by positive sodium ions rapidly passing into the axon.</dd>
<dt id="desmosome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Desmosome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desmosome">desmosome</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called&nbsp;<strong>macula adhaerens</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A cell structure specialized for cell-to-cell adhesion.</dd>
<dt id="developmental_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Developmental biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_biology">developmental biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the processes by which living organisms grow and develop over time. The field may also encompass the study of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;reproduction">reproduction</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#regeneration"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;regeneration">regeneration</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metamorphosis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metamorphosis">metamorphosis</span></a>, and the growth and differentiation of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#stem_cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;stem cell">stem cells</span></a>&nbsp;in mature tissues.</dd>
<dt id="disease" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Disease" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease">disease</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="dna" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="DNA" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA">DNA</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">deoxyribonucleic acid</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="dna_replication" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="DNA replication" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_replication">DNA replication</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The replication of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;molecule; the process of producing two identical copies from one original DNA molecule, in which the double helix is unwound and each strand acts as a template for the next strand; nucleotide bases are matched to synthesize the new partner strands.</dd>
<dt id="dna_sequencing" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="DNA sequencing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_sequencing">DNA sequencing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of determining the precise order of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotides" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotides">nucleotides</a>&nbsp;within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;molecule.</dd>
<dt id="drug" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Drug" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drug">drug</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="dynein" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Dynein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynein">dynein</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A motor protein (also called molecular motor or motor molecule) in cells which converts the chemical energy contained in ATP into the mechanical energy of movement.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="E" class="mw-headline">E</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="ecological_efficiency" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecological efficiency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_efficiency">ecological efficiency</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The efficiency with which energy is transferred from one&nbsp;<a title="Trophic level" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_level">trophic level</a>&nbsp;to the next. It is determined by a combination of efficiencies relating to organismic resource acquisition and assimilation in an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#ecosystem"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;ecosystem">ecosystem</span></a>.&nbsp;<a title="Primary production" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_production">Primary production</a>&nbsp;occurs in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#autotroph"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;autotroph">autotrophic</span></a>&nbsp;organisms of an ecosystem.</dd>
<dt id="ecological_pyramid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecological pyramid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_pyramid">ecological pyramid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An ecological pyramid (also trophic pyramid, eltonian pyramid, energy pyramid, or sometimes food pyramid) is a graphical representation designed to show the biomass or bio productivity at each trophic level in a given ecosystem. Biomass is the amount of living or organic matter present in an organism.</dd>
<dt id="ecological_succession" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecological succession" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_succession">ecological succession</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The more or less predictable and orderly set of changes that occurs in the composition or structure of an ecological community over time.</dd>
<dt id="ecology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecology">ecology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The scientific analysis and study of interactions between&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organism">organisms</span></a>&nbsp;and their&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#environment"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;environment">environment</span></a>. It is an interdisciplinary field that includes biology,&nbsp;<a title="Geography" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography">geography</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Earth science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_science">Earth science</a>.</dd>
<dt id="ecophysiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecophysiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecophysiology">ecophysiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biological" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological">biological</a>&nbsp;discipline that studies the adaptation of an organism's physiology to environmental conditions.</dd>
<dt id="ecosystem" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecosystem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem">ecosystem</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Community (ecology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_(ecology)">community</a>&nbsp;of living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organism">organisms</span></a>&nbsp;in conjunction with the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#abiotic_component"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;abiotic component">non-living components</span></a>&nbsp;of their physical environment, interacting as a system.</dd>
<dt id="ecotype" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecotype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecotype">ecotype</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Sometimes called an&nbsp;<strong>ecospecies</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">In evolutionary ecology, a genetically distinct geographic variety,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#population"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;population">population</span></a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Race (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(biology)">race</a>&nbsp;within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>&nbsp;which is adapted to specific environmental conditions.</dd>
<dt id="ectoderm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ectoderm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ectoderm">ectoderm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The outermost layer of cells or tissue of an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>&nbsp;in early development, or the parts derived from this, which include the&nbsp;<a title="Epidermis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epidermis">epidermis</a>, nerve tissue, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nephridia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nephridia">nephridia</a>.</dd>
<dt id="ectotherm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ectotherm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ectotherm">ectotherm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organism in which internal physiological sources of heat are of relatively small or quite negligible importance in controlling&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Body temperature" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_temperature">body temperature</a>. Colloquially, these organisms often referred to as "cold-blooded".</dd>
<dt id="effector" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Effector (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effector_(biology)">effector</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small molecule that selectively binds to a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">protein</span></a>&nbsp;and regulates its&nbsp;<a title="Biological activity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_activity">biological activity</a>. In this manner, effector molecules act as&nbsp;<a title="Ligand (biochemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligand_(biochemistry)">ligands</a>&nbsp;that can increase or decrease&nbsp;<a title="Allosteric regulation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allosteric_regulation">enzyme activity</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Gene expression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_expression">gene expression</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Cell signaling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_signaling">cell signaling</a>.</dd>
<dt id="efferent" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">efferent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Conducted or conducting outwards or away from something (for nerves, the central nervous system; for blood vessels, the organ supplied). Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#afferent"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;afferent">afferent</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="egg" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Egg (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egg_(biology)">egg</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The organic vessel containing the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#zygote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;zygote">zygote</span></a>&nbsp;in which an animal&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>&nbsp;develops until it can survive on its own, at which point the developing organism emerges from the egg in a process known as&nbsp;<em>hatching</em>.</dd>
<dt id="electrochemical_gradient" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electrochemical gradient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrochemical_gradient">electrochemical gradient</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A gradient of&nbsp;<a title="Electrochemical potential" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrochemical_potential">electrochemical potential</a>, usually for an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#ion"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;ion">ion</span></a>&nbsp;that can move across a membrane. The gradient consists of two parts: the electrical potential and the difference in chemical concentration across the membrane.</dd>
<dt id="electromagnetic_spectrum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electromagnetic spectrum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_spectrum">electromagnetic spectrum</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The range of all possible frequencies of&nbsp;<a title="Electromagnetic radiation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation">electromagnetic radiation</a>. When referring to an object, the electromagnetic spectrum is the characteristic distribution of electromagnetic radiation emitted or absorbed by that particular object.</dd>
<dt id="electron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron">electron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A negatively charged subatomic particle, symbolized by&nbsp;<em>e<sup>&minus;</sup></em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>&beta;<sup>&minus;</sup></em>.</dd>
<dt id="electron_acceptor" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron acceptor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_acceptor">electron acceptor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An electron acceptor is a chemical entity that accepts electrons transferred to it from another compound. It is an oxidizing agent that, by virtue of its accepting electrons, is itself reduced in the process.</dd>
<dt id="electron_carrier" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Electron carrier" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_carrier">electron carrier</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">electron carrier. Any of various molecules that are capable of accepting one or two electrons from one molecule and donating them to another in the process of electron transport. As the electrons are transferred from one electron carrier to another, their energy level decreases, and energy is released.</dd>
<dt id="electron_donor" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron donor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_donor">electron donor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An electron donor is a chemical entity that donates electrons to another compound. It is a reducing agent that, by virtue of its donating electrons, is itself oxidized in the process.</dd>
<dt id="electron_microscope" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron microscope" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_microscope">electron microscope</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The electron microscope is a type of microscope that uses a beam of electrons to create an image of the specimen. It is capable of much higher magnifications and has a greater resolving power than a light microscope, allowing it to see much smaller objects in finer detail.</dd>
<dt id="electron_transport_chain" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Electron transport chain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_transport_chain">electron transport chain</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The site in a mitochondrion of&nbsp;<a title="Oxidative phosphorylation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxidative_phosphorylation">oxidative phosphorylation</a>&nbsp;in eukaryotes. The NADH and succinate generated by the&nbsp;<a title="Citric acid cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citric_acid_cycle">citric acid cycle</a>&nbsp;are oxidized, providing energy to power ATP synthase. Photosynthetic electron transport chain of the thylakoid membrane.</dd>
<dt id="embryo" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Embryo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryo">embryo</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A developing stage of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#multicellular_organism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;multicellular organism">multicellular organism</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="embryology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Embryology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryology">embryology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the development of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#gamete"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;gamete">gametes</span></a>&nbsp;(sex cells), fertilization, and development of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryos</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fetus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fetus">fetuses</span></a>. Additionally, embryology involves the study of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Congenital disorder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congenital_disorder">congenital disorders</a>&nbsp;that occur before birth.</dd>
<dt id="endangered_species" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endangered species" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endangered_species">endangered species</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Endangered species are threatened by factors such as habitat loss, hunting, disease and climate change, and usually, endangered species, have a declining population or a very limited range.</dd>
<dt id="endemism" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endemism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemism">endemism</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The ecological state of an organism or species being unique to a defined geographic location, such as an island, nation, country, habitat type, or other defined zone. Organisms are said to be&nbsp;<em>endemic</em>&nbsp;to a place if they are indigenous to it and found nowhere else.</dd>
<dt id="endergonic_reaction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endergonic reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endergonic_reaction">endergonic reaction</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called a&nbsp;<strong>nonspontaneous reaction</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>unfavorable reaction</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a title="Chemical reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_reaction">chemical reaction</a>&nbsp;in which the standard change in&nbsp;<a title="Gibbs free energy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibbs_free_energy">free energy</a>&nbsp;is positive, and energy is absorbed.</dd>
<dt id="endocrine_gland" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endocrine gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocrine_gland">endocrine gland</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gland">gland</a>&nbsp;of the animalian&nbsp;<a title="Endocrine system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocrine_system">endocrine system</a>&nbsp;that secretes&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#hormone"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;hormone">hormones</span></a>&nbsp;directly into the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#blood"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;blood">blood</span></a>&nbsp;rather than through a duct. In humans, the major glands of the endocrine system include the&nbsp;<a title="Pineal gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pineal_gland">pineal gland</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pituitary gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pituitary_gland">pituitary gland</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pancreas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pancreas">pancreas</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ovaries" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovaries">ovaries</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Testes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testes">testes</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Thyroid gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thyroid_gland">thyroid gland</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Parathyroid gland" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parathyroid_gland">parathyroid gland</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Hypothalamus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothalamus">hypothalamus</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Adrenal glands" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrenal_glands">adrenal glands</a>.</dd>
<dt id="endocrine_system" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endocrine system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocrine_system">endocrine system</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The collection of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#endocrine_gland"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;endocrine gland">glands</span></a>&nbsp;that produce&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#hormone"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;hormone">hormones</span></a>&nbsp;which regulate&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metabolism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metabolism">metabolism</span></a>, growth and development, tissue function, and a wide variety of other biological processes.</dd>
<dt id="endocytosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endocytosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocytosis">endocytosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A form of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#active_transport"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;active transport">active transport</span></a>&nbsp;in which a cell transports molecules such as proteins into the cell's interior by engulfing them in an energy-consuming process.</dd>
<dt id="endoderm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endoderm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endoderm">endoderm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the three primary germ layers in the very early human&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>.
