The other two layers are the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#ectoderm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;ectoderm">ectoderm</span></a>&nbsp;(outside layer) and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#mesoderm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;mesoderm">mesoderm</span></a>&nbsp;(middle layer), with the endoderm being the innermost layer.</dd>
<dt id="endogenous" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Endogenous" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endogenous">endogenous</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of a substance or process) Originating from within a system (such as an organism, tissue, or cell), as with&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Endocannabinoid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocannabinoid">endogenous cannabinoids</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#circadian_rhythm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;circadian rhythm">circadian rhythms</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#exogenous"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;exogenous">exogenous</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="endoplasmic_reticulum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endoplasmic reticulum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endoplasmic_reticulum">endoplasmic reticulum</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a title="Organelle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organelle">organelle</a>&nbsp;found in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotic cells" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic_cells">eukaryotic cells</a>&nbsp;that forms an interconnected network of flattened, membrane-enclosed sacs or tube-like structures known as cisternae.</dd>
<dt id="endosperm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endosperm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosperm">endosperm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The tissue produced inside the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Seeds" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seeds">seeds</a>&nbsp;of most of the flowering plants following&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Fertilization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertilization">fertilization</a>.</dd>
<dt id="endosymbiotic_theory" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Endosymbiotic theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosymbiotic_theory">endosymbiotic theory</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An evolutionary theory of the origin of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotic cells" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic_cells">eukaryotic cells</a>&nbsp;from&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Prokaryotic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryotic">prokaryotic</a>&nbsp;organisms, first articulated in 1905 and 1910 by the Russian botanist&nbsp;<a title="Konstantin Mereschkowski" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konstantin_Mereschkowski">Konstantin Mereschkowski</a>, and advanced and substantiated with microbiological evidence by&nbsp;<a title="Lynn Margulis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynn_Margulis">Lynn Margulis</a>&nbsp;in 1967.</dd>
<dt id="endotherm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Endotherm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endotherm">endotherm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organism that maintains its body at a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Metabolically" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metabolically">metabolically</a>&nbsp;favorable temperature, largely by the use of heat set free by its internal bodily functions instead of relying almost purely on ambient heat.</dd>
<dt id="entomology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Entomology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entomology">entomology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Entomology is the study of insects, but etymology is the study of words.</dd>
<dt id="environmental_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_biology">environmental biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">the branch of biology concerned with the relations between organisms and their environment. bionomics, ecology. biological science, biology - the science that studies living organisms. palaeoecology, paleoecology - the branch of ecology that studies ancient ecology.</dd>
<dt id="enzyme" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Enzyme" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzyme">enzyme</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Enzymes are biological molecules (proteins) that act as catalysts and help complex reactions occur everywhere in life. Let's say you ate a piece of meat. Proteases would go to work and help break down the peptide bonds between the amino acids.</dd>
<dt id="epidemiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Epidemiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epidemiology">epidemiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Epidemiology is the study and analysis of the patterns, causes, and effects of health and disease conditions in defined populations. It is the cornerstone of public health, and shapes policy decisions and evidence-based practice by identifying risk factors for disease and targets for preventive healthcare.</dd>
<dt id="epigenetics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Epigenetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epigenetics">epigenetics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sub-field of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#genetics"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;genetics">genetics</span></a>&nbsp;that studies cellular and physiological phenotypic trait variations caused by external or environmental factors which affect how cells&nbsp;<a title="Gene expression" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_expression">express</a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#gene"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;gene">genes</span></a>, as opposed to those caused by changes in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;sequence.</dd>
<dt id="epiphyte" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Epiphyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epiphyte">epiphyte</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organism that grows on the surface of a&nbsp;<a title="Plant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant">plant</a>&nbsp;and derives its&nbsp;<a title="Moisture" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moisture">moisture</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nutrients" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nutrients">nutrients</a>&nbsp;from the air, rain, marine environments or from debris accumulating around it.</dd>
<dt id="essential_nutrient" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Essential nutrient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Essential_nutrient">essential nutrient</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="estrogen" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Estrogen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estrogen">estrogen</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The primary female sex&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#hormone"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;hormone">hormone</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="ethology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ethology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethology">ethology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The scientific study of non-human animal behaviour (i.e. excluding human behaviour) and usually with a focus on behaviour under natural conditions, and viewing behaviour as an evolutionarily adaptive trait.</dd>
<dt id="eukaryote" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Eukaryote" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote">eukaryote</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Organisms whose cells have a&nbsp;<a title="Cell nucleus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus">nucleus</a>&nbsp;enclosed within&nbsp;<a title="Cell membrane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_membrane">membranes</a>, unlike&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Prokaryotes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryotes">Prokaryotes</a>&nbsp;(Bacteria and other Archaea).</dd>
<dt id="evolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolution">evolution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The change in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#heredity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;heredity">heritable</span></a>&nbsp;characteristics of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#population"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;population">populations</span></a>&nbsp;of biological organisms over successive&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#generation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;generation">generations</span></a>, which may occur by&nbsp;<a title="Mutation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation">mutation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Gene flow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_flow">gene flow</a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#natural_selection"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;natural selection">natural selection</span></a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Genetic drift" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_drift">random chance</a>.</dd>
<dt id="evolutionary_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Evolutionary biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_biology">evolutionary biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Evolutionary biology is the subfield of biology that studies the evolutionary processes that produced the diversity of life on Earth starting from a single origin of life. These processes include the descent of species, and the origin of new species.</dd>
<dt id="exocytosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Exocytosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exocytosis">exocytosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A form of active transport and bulk transport in which a cell transports&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Molecules" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecules">molecules</a>&nbsp;out of the cell by expelling them through an energy-dependent process.</dd>
<dt id="exogenous" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Exogenous" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exogenous">exogenous</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of a substance or process) Originating outside of or external to a system (such as an organism, tissue, or cell), as with&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#drug"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;drug">drugs</span></a>&nbsp;and many&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#pathogen"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;pathogen">pathogens</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#endogenous"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;endogenous">endogenous</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="exponential_growth" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Exponential growth" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exponential_growth">exponential growth</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">It is exhibited when the rate of change of the value of a mathematical function is proportional to the function's current value, resulting in its value at any time being an exponential function of time.</dd>
<dt id="external_fertilization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="External fertilization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/External_fertilization">external fertilization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fertilization"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fertilization">fertilization</span></a>&nbsp;in which a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#sperm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;sperm">sperm</span></a>&nbsp;unites with an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#egg"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;egg">egg</span></a>&nbsp;external to the body or bodies of the parent organisms. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#internal_fertilization"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;internal fertilization">internal fertilization</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="extinction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Extinction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinction">extinction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="extracellular" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Extracellular" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extracellular">extracellular</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of or occurring in the space outside the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">plasma membrane</span></a>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#intracellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;intracellular">intracellular</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="extranuclear_inheritance" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Extranuclear inheritance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extranuclear_inheritance">extranuclear inheritance</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A transmission of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genes">genes</a>&nbsp;that take place outside the&nbsp;<a title="Cell nucleus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus">nucleus</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="F" class="mw-headline">F</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="facultative_anaerobe" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Facultative anaerobic organism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facultative_anaerobic_organism">facultative anaerobe</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organism which is capable of producing&nbsp;<a title="Energy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy">energy</a>&nbsp;through&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Aerobic respiration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerobic_respiration">aerobic respiration</a>&nbsp;and then switching to&nbsp;<a title="Anaerobic respiration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaerobic_respiration">anaerobic respiration</a>&nbsp;depending on the amounts of oxygen and fermentable material in the environment.</dd>
<dt id="family" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Family (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_(biology)">family</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="fermentation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Fermentation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermentation">fermentation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metabolism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metabolism">metabolic</span></a>&nbsp;process that consumes&nbsp;<a title="Sugar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sugar">sugar</a>&nbsp;in the absence of&nbsp;<a title="Oxygen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen">oxygen</a>.</dd>
<dt id="fitness" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Fitness (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitness_(biology)">fitness</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="fitness_landscape" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Fitness landscape" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitness_landscape">fitness landscape</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="fertilization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Fertilization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertilization">fertilization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="fetus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Fetus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fetus">fetus</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also spelled&nbsp;<strong>foetus</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">An animal&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>&nbsp;after eight weeks of development.</dd>
<dt id="flagellum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Flagellum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellum">flagellum</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"><em>(pl.)</em>&nbsp;<strong>flagella</strong></span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">A lash-like appendage that protrudes from the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>&nbsp;body of certain bacterial and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic">eukaryotic</a>&nbsp;cells.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="flavin_adenine_dinucleotide_(fad)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Flavin adenine dinucleotide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flavin_adenine_dinucleotide">flavin adenine dinucleotide</a>&nbsp;(FAD)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Redox cofactor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redox_cofactor">redox cofactor</a>, more specifically a prosthetic group of a protein, involved in different important&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Enzymatic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzymatic">enzymatic</a>&nbsp;reactions in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metabolism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metabolism">metabolism</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="food_chain" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Food chain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_chain">food chain</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The chain of eating and getting nutrition which starts from a small herbivores animal and ends up at a big carnivorous organism.</dd>
<dt id="founder_effect" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Founder effect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founder_effect">founder effect</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A loss of genetic variation that takes places when a new&nbsp;<a title="Population" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population">population</a>&nbsp;is established by a very small number of individuals from a larger population.</dd>
<dt id="fungi" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi">fungi</a></dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<h2><span id="G" class="mw-headline">G</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="g_protein" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="G protein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G_protein">G protein</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A family of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">proteins</span></a>&nbsp;that act as molecular switches inside&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>, and are implicated in transmitting signals from a diversity of stimuli outside a cell to its interior.</dd>
<dt id="gamete" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Gamete" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamete">gamete</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="gene" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Gene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene">gene</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any segment of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;that contains the information necessary to produce a functional&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;and/or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">protein</span></a>&nbsp;product in a controlled manner. Genes are often considered the fundamental molecular units of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#heredity"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;heredity">heredity</span></a>. The transmission of genes from a parent cell or organism to its&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>&nbsp;is the basis of the inheritance of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#trait"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;trait">phenotypic traits</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="gene_pool" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Gene pool" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_pool">gene pool</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A set of all&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genes">genes</a>, or genetic information, in any population, usually of a particular&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="generation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">generation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="genetic_code" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genetic code" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_code">genetic code</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A set of rules used by living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>&nbsp;to translate information encoded within&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic material" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_material">genetic material</a>&nbsp;(DNA or mRNA sequences) into proteins.</dd>
<dt id="genetic_drift" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genetic drift" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_drift">genetic drift</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alteration in the frequency of an existing&nbsp;<a title="Gene" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene">gene</a>&nbsp;variant in a population due to random sampling of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Organisms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisms">organisms</a>.</dd>
<dt id="genetic_variation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genetic variation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_variation">genetic variation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Variations of&nbsp;<a title="Genome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome">genomes</a>&nbsp;between members of species, or between groups of species thriving in different parts of the world as a result of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic mutation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_mutation">genetic mutation</a>. Genetic diversity in a population or species is a result of new gene combinations (e.g.&nbsp;<a title="Chromosomal crossover" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosomal_crossover">crossing over of chromosomes</a>), genetic mutations,&nbsp;<a title="Genetic drift" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_drift">genetic drift</a>, etc.</dd>
<dt id="genetics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genetics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetics">genetics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of heredity.</dd>
<dt id="genome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome">genome</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The entire set of genetic material contained within the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#chromosome"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;chromosome">chromosomes</span></a>&nbsp;of an organism,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#organelle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;organelle">organelle</span></a>, or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#virus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;virus">virus</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="genotype" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genotype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genotype">genotype</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Part of the genetic makeup of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>, and therefore of an organism or individual, which determines one of its characteristics (phenotype).</dd>
<dt id="genus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Genus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genus">genus</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="gizzard" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Gizzard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gizzard">gizzard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organ found in the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Digestive tract" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digestive_tract">digestive tract</a>&nbsp;of some animals, including&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Archosaurs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archosaurs">archosaurs</a>&nbsp;(pterosaurs, crocodiles, alligators, and dinosaurs, including birds), earthworms, some&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gastropods" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gastropods">gastropods</a>, some&nbsp;<a title="Fish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish">fish</a>, and some&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Crustaceans" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crustaceans">crustaceans</a>.</dd>
<dt id="guanine" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Guanine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guanine">guanine</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the four main&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleobases" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleobases">nucleobases</a>&nbsp;found in the nucleic acids&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>, the others being&nbsp;<a title="Adenine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adenine">adenine</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Cytosine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytosine">cytosine</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Thymine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thymine">thymine</a>&nbsp;(uracil in RNA).</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="H" class="mw-headline">H</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="habitat" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Habitat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat">habitat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A place for animals, people, and plants and non-living things.</dd>
<dt id="habituation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Habituation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habituation">habituation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A form of learning in which an&nbsp;<a title="Organism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organism">organism</a>&nbsp;decreases or desists its responses to a stimulus after repeated or prolonged presentations .</dd>
<dt id="heredity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Heredity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heredity">heredity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The passing on of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#phenotype"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;phenotype">phenotypic</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#trait"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;trait">traits</span></a>&nbsp;from parents to their&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>, either through&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#sexual_reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;sexual reproduction">sexual</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#asexual_reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;asexual reproduction">asexual reproduction</span></a>. Offspring cells and organisms are said to&nbsp;<em>inherit</em>&nbsp;the genetic information of their parents.</dd>
<dt id="hermaphrodite" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Hermaphrodite" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermaphrodite">hermaphrodite</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sexually reproducing organism with both male and female&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Reproductive organ" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reproductive_organ">reproductive organs</a>.</dd>
<dt id="herpetology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Herpetology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herpetology">herpetology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#zoology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;zoology">zoology</span></a>&nbsp;that studies&nbsp;<a title="Reptile" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptile">reptiles</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Amphibian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian">amphibians</a>.</dd>
<dt id="heterosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Heterosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterosis">heterosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The improved or increased function of any biological quality in a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#hybrid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;hybrid">hybrid</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="heterotroph" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Heterotroph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotroph">heterotroph</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="histology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Histology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Histology">histology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the microscopic anatomy of cells and tissues of plants and animals.</dd>
<dt id="hormone" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Hormone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hormone">hormone</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any member of a class of signaling molecules produced by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Glands" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glands">glands</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#multicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;multicellular">multicellular</span></a>&nbsp;organisms that are transported by the circulatory system to target distant organs to regulate physiology and behaviour.</dd>
<dt id="host" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Host (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_(biology)">host</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any living organism that harbors another living organism (known as a "guest" or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#symbiont"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;symbiont">symbiont</span></a>), whether the guest is&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#parasite"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;parasite">parasitic</span></a>,&nbsp;<a title="Mutualism (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutualism_(biology)">mutualistic</a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Commensalism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commensalism">commensalist</a>&nbsp;in its interactions with the host. The guest typically receives shelter and nourishment from the host.</dd>
<dt id="hybrid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Hybrid (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)">hybrid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="hydrocarbon" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Hydrocarbon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organic compound consisting entirely of hydrogen and carbon atoms. Hydrocarbons from which one hydrogen atom has been removed are functional groups called hydrocarbyls.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="I" class="mw-headline">I</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="ichthyology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ichthyology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ichthyology">ichthyology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology devoted to the study of&nbsp;<a title="Fish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish">fish</a>, including bony fishes (Osteichthyes), cartilaginous fish (Chondrichthyes), and jawless fish (Agnatha).</dd>
<dt id="immune_response" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Immune response" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immune_response">immune response</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The immune response is how your body recognizes and defends itself against bacteria, viruses, and substances that appear foreign and harmful.</dd>
<dt id="immunity" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Immunity (medical)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunity_(medical)">immunity</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="immunogloblin" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Immunogloblin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunogloblin">immunogloblin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Glycoprotein molecules produced by plasma cells (white blood cells) which act as a critical part of the immune response by specifically recognizing and binding to particular&nbsp;<a title="Antigen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigen">antigens</a>, such as bacteria or viruses, and aiding in their destruction. Also known as&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Antibodies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antibodies">antibodies</a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="infection" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Infection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infection">infection</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The invasion of an organism's cells or tissues by a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#disease"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;disease">disease</span></a>-causing&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#pathogen"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;pathogen">pathogen</span></a>, its growth and/or multiplication, and the reaction of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#host"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;host">host</span></a>&nbsp;organism to the infectious agent and the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#toxin"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;toxin">toxins</span></a>&nbsp;it produces. The variety of biological pathogens capable of causing infections includes certain&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#bacteria"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;bacteria">bacteria</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#virus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;virus">viruses</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fungi"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fungi">fungi</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protist"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protist">protists</span></a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Parasitic worms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitic_worms">parasitic worms</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Arthropod" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthropod">arthropods</a>.</dd>
<dt id="insulin" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Insulin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insulin">insulin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Insulin helps keeps your blood sugar level from getting too high (hyperglycemia) or too low (hypoglycemia). ... After you eat food and your blood sugar level rises, cells in your pancreas (known as beta cells) are signaled to release insulin into your bloodstream.</dd>
<dt id="integrative_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Integrative biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrative_biology">integrative biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The various forms of cross-disciplinary and multitaxon research.</dd>
<dt id="interferon" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Interferon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interferon">interferon</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of signaling proteins made and released by host cells in response to the presence of several pathogens, such as viruses, bacteria, parasites, and also tumor cells. In a typical scenario, a virus-infected cell will release interferons causing nearby cells to heighten their antiviral defenses.</dd>
<dt id="internal_fertilization" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Internal fertilization" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_fertilization">internal fertilization</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#fertilization"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;fertilization">fertilization</span></a>&nbsp;which takes place inside the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#egg"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;egg">egg</span></a>-producing individual.</dd>
<dt id="international_system_of_units" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="International System of Units" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_System_of_Units">International System of Units</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(French:&nbsp;<em>Syst&egrave;me international d'unit&eacute;s</em>; abbreviated SI) The modern form of the metric system, and the most widely used system of measurement.</dd>
<dt id="interphase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Interphase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interphase">interphase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="intracellular" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Intracellular" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intracellular">intracellular</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of or occurring inside or within the enclosed interior of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>. Contrast&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#extracellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;extracellular">extracellular</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="introduced_species" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Introduced species" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Introduced_species">introduced species</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="invertebrate" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Invertebrate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invertebrate">invertebrate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of animals that have no backbone, unlike animals such as reptiles, amphibians, fish, birds and mammals, which all have a backbone.</dd>
<dt id="ion" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ion">ion</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An atom or molecule with a net electric charge due to the loss or gain of one or more electrons.</dd>
<dt id="ionic_bond" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Ionic bond" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionic_bond">ionic bond</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The complete transfer of valence electron(s) between atoms. It is a type of chemical bond that generates two oppositely charged ions. In ionic bonds, the metal loses electrons to become a positively charged cation, whereas the nonmetal accepts those electrons to become a negatively charged anion.</dd>
<dt id="isomer" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Isomer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isomer">isomer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A molecule with the same chemical formula as another molecule, but with a different chemical structure. That is, isomers contain the same number of atoms of each element, but have different arrangements of their atoms.</dd>
<dt id="isotonic_solution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Isotonic solutions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isotonic_solutions">isotonic solution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Refers to two solutions having the same osmotic pressure across a semipermeable membrane. This state allows for the free movement of water across the membrane without changing the concentration of solutes on either side.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="J" class="mw-headline">J</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="jejunum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Jejunum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jejunum">jejunum</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The midsection of the small intestine of many higher vertebrates like mammals, birds, and reptiles. It is present between the&nbsp;<a title="Duodenum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duodenum">duodenum</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title="Ileum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ileum">ileum</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="K" class="mw-headline">K</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="kinase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Kinase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinase">kinase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#enzyme"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;enzyme">enzyme</span></a>&nbsp;that catalyzes the transfer of phosphate groups from high-energy, phosphate-donating molecules to specific substrates.</dd>
<dt id="kingdom" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Kingdom (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)">kingdom</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="krebs_cycle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Krebs cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krebs_cycle">Krebs cycle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#citric_acid_cycle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;citric acid cycle">citric acid cycle</span></a></em>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="L" class="mw-headline">L</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="larva" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Larva" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larva">larva</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><em>(pl.)</em>&nbsp;<strong>larvae</strong></dd>
<dd class="glossary">A distinct juvenile form many&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#animal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;animal">animals</span></a>&nbsp;undergo before&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metamorphosis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metamorphosis">metamorphosis</span></a>&nbsp;into adults. Animals with indirect development, such as insects, amphibians, or cnidarians, typically have a larval phase of their&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#life_cycle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;life cycle">life cycle</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="law_of_independent_assortment" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Law of Independent Assortment" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_Independent_Assortment">Law of Independent Assortment</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The principle, originally formulated by&nbsp;<a title="Gregor Mendel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregor_Mendel">Gregor Mendel</a>, stating that when two or more characteristics are inherited, individual hereditary factors assort independently during gamete production, giving different traits an equal opportunity of occurring together.</dd>
<dt id="leukocyte" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Leukocyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leukocyte">leukocyte</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A colourless cell which circulates in the blood and body fluids and is involved in counteracting foreign substances and disease; sometimes called a&nbsp;<em>white blood cell</em>. There are several types, all amoeboid cells with a nucleus, including lymphocytes, granulocytes, and monocytes.</dd>
<dt id="lichen" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Lichen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lichen">lichen</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="life" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Life" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life">life</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="life_cycle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Biological life cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle">life cycle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="ligament" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ligament" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligament">ligament</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The fibrous connective tissue that connects bones to other bones and is also known as&nbsp;<em>articular ligament</em>,&nbsp;<em>articular larua</em>,&nbsp;<em>fibrous ligament</em>, or&nbsp;<em>true ligament</em>.</dd>
<dt id="light-independent_reactions" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Light-independent reactions" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-independent_reactions">light-independent reactions</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#calvin_cycle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;Calvin cycle">Calvin cycle</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="linked_genes" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Linked genes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linked_genes">linked genes</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any set of one or more&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#gene"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;gene">genes</span></a>&nbsp;which are sufficiently close together on the same chromosome that they are very unlikely to assort independently and therefore are usually inherited together.</dd>
<dt id="lipid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Lipid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipid">lipid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A substance that is insoluble in water and soluble in alcohol, ether, and chloroform. Lipids are an important component of living cells. Together with carbohydrates and proteins, lipids are the main constituents of plant and animal cells. Cholesterol and triglycerides are lipids.</dd>
<dt id="lipoprotein" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Lipoprotein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipoprotein">lipoprotein</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A biochemical assembly that contains both proteins and lipids, bound to the proteins, which allow fats to move through the water inside and outside cells. The proteins serve to emulsify the lipid molecules.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="M" class="mw-headline">M</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="m_phase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="M phase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M_phase">M phase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mitosis and cytokinesis together define the mitotic (M) phase of an animal cell cycle &ndash; the division of the mother cell into two daughter cells, genetically identical to each other and to their parent cell.</dd>
<dt id="macroevolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Macroevolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macroevolution">macroevolution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Evolution on a scale of separated gene pools. Macroevolutionary studies focus on change that occurs at or above the level of species, in contrast with microevolution, which refers to smaller evolutionary changes (typically described as changes in allele frequencies) within a species or population.</dd>
<dt id="macromolecule" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Macromolecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macromolecule">macromolecule</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A very large molecule, such as a protein, commonly created by polymerization of smaller subunits (monomers). They are typically composed of thousands or more atoms.</dd>
<dt id="macronutrient" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Macronutrient" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macronutrient">macronutrient</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Nutrients needed in large amounts which provide calories or energy. Nutrients are substances needed for growth, metabolism, and for other body functions. There are three basic types of macronutrients: fats, proteins, and carbohydrates.</dd>
<dt id="macrophage" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Macrophage" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macrophage">macrophage</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A kind of swallowing cell, which means it functions by literally swallowing up other particles or smaller cells. Macrophages engulf and digest debris (like dead cells) and foreign particles through the process of&nbsp;<a title="Phagocytosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagocytosis">phagocytosis</a>, so macrophages act like scavengers.</dd>
<dt id="mammalogy" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mammalogy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammalogy">mammalogy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of mammals, a class of vertebrates with characteristics such as homeothermic metabolism, fur, four-chambered hearts, and complex nervous systems.</dd>
<dt id="marine_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Marine biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marine_biology">marine biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of organisms in the ocean or other marine bodies of water. Given that in biology many phyla, families and genera have some species that live in the sea and others that live on land, marine biology classifies species based on the environment rather than on taxonomy.</dd>
<dt id="mast_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mast cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mast_cell">mast cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cell filled with basophil granules, found in numbers in connective tissue and releasing histamine and other substances during inflammatory and allergic reactions.</dd>
<dt id="mating" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mating" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mating">mating</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="medulla" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Medulla oblongata" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medulla_oblongata">medulla</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The continuation of the spinal cord within the skull, forming the lowest part of the brainstem and containing control centres for the heart and lungs.</dd>
<dt id="meiosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Meiosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meiosis">meiosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A specialized type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_division"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell division">cell division</span></a>&nbsp;in which a dividing parent cell proceeds through two consecutive divisions, ultimately producing four genetically unique daughter cells in each of which the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#chromosome"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;chromosome">chromosome</span></a>&nbsp;number is half of that in the original parent cell. This process is exclusive to cells of the sex organs in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#sexual_reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;sexual reproduction">sexually reproducing</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#eukaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;eukaryote">eukaryotes</span></a>, where it serves the purpose of generating&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#gamete"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;gamete">gametes</span></a>&nbsp;such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#egg"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;egg">eggs</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#sperm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;sperm">sperm</span></a>, or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#spore"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;spore">spores</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="membrane_potential" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Membrane potential" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Membrane_potential">membrane potential</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">When a nerve or muscle cell is at "rest", its membrane potential is called the resting membrane potential. In a typical neuron, this is about &ndash;70 millivolts (mV). The minus sign indicates that the inside of the cell is negative with respect to the surrounding extracellular fluid.</dd>
<dt id="messenger_rna" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Messenger RNA" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messenger_RNA">messenger RNA</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large family of RNA molecules that convey genetic information from DNA to the ribosome.</dd>
<dt id="metabolism" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Metabolism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metabolism">metabolism</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="metamorphosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Metamorphosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamorphosis">metamorphosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="metaphase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Metaphase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaphase">metaphase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The third phase of mitosis, in which duplicated genetic material carried in the nucleus of a parent cell is separated into two identical daughter cells. During metaphase, the cell's chromosomes align themselves in the middle of the cell through a type of cellular "tug of war".</dd>
<dt id="microbiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Microbiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microbiology">microbiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of microscopic organisms, such as bacteria, viruses, archaea, fungi and protozoa. This discipline includes fundamental research on the biochemistry, physiology, cell biology, ecology, evolution and clinical aspects of microorganisms, including the host response to these agents.</dd>
<dt id="microevolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Microevolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microevolution">microevolution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The alteration in&nbsp;<a title="Allele" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allele">allele</a>&nbsp;frequencies that occurs over time within a population.</dd>
<dt id="mitochondria" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Mitochondria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondria">mitochondria</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"><em>(sing.)</em>&nbsp;<strong>mitochondrion</strong></span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="mitosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mitosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitosis">mitosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#eukaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;eukaryote">eukaryotic</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>, the part of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_cycle"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell cycle">cell cycle</span></a>&nbsp;during which the division of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleus">nucleus</span></a>&nbsp;takes place and duplicated&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#chromosome"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;chromosome">chromosomes</span></a>&nbsp;are separated into two distinct nuclei. Mitosis is generally preceded by the "S" stage of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#interphase"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;interphase">interphase</span></a>, when the cell's&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;is&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA_replication"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA replication">replicated</span></a>, and followed by&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytokinesis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytokinesis">cytokinesis</span></a>, when the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytoplasm"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytoplasm">cytoplasm</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell_membrane"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell membrane">cell membrane</span></a>&nbsp;are divided into two new daughter cells. It is similar to but distinct from&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#binary_fission"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;binary fission">binary fission</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#meiosis"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;meiosis">meiosis</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="molecule" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Molecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecule">molecule</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The smallest particle in a chemical element or compound that has the chemical properties of that element or compound. Molecules are made up of atoms that are held together by chemical bonds. These bonds form as a result of the sharing or exchange of electrons among atoms.</dd>
<dt id="molecular_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Molecular biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_biology">molecular biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology concerning biological activity at the molecular level. The field of molecular biology overlaps with biology and chemistry and in particular with genetics and biochemistry.</dd>
<dt id="molecular_switch" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Molecular switch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_switch">molecular switch</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A molecule that can be reversibly changed between two or more stable states.</dd>
<dt id="monomer" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Monomer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monomer">monomer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Molecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecule">molecule</a>&nbsp;that "can undergo polymerization thereby contributing constitutional units to the essential structure of a macromolecule".</dd>
<dt id="morphology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Morphology (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology)">morphology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="motile" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Motility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motility">motile</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="motor_neuron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Motor neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motor_neuron">motor neuron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A neuron whose cell body is situated in the motor&nbsp;<a title="Motor cortex" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motor_cortex">cortex</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Brainstem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brainstem">brainstem</a>&nbsp;or the&nbsp;<a title="Spinal cord" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spinal_cord">spinal cord</a>, and whose axon (fiber) projects to the spinal cord or outside of the spinal cord to directly or indirectly control effector organs, mainly muscles and glands.</dd>
<dt id="mucous_membrane" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mucous membrane" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mucous_membrane">mucous membrane</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A membrane that lines various cavities in the body and covers the surface of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Internal organs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_organs">internal organs</a>.</dd>
<dt id="multicellular" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Multicellular organism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellular_organism">multicellular</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Having or consisting of more than one&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>, as opposed to being&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#unicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;unicellular">unicellular</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="mycology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Mycology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mycology">mycology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology concerned with the study of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi">fungi</a>, including their genetic and biochemical properties, their taxonomy and their use to humans as a source for tinder, medicine, food, and entheogens, as well as their dangers, such as poisoning or infection.</dd>
<dt id="myofibril" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Myofibril" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myofibril">myofibril</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A basic rod-like unit of a muscle&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="myosin" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Myosin" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myosin">myosin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A superfamily of motor&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">proteins</span></a>&nbsp;best known for their roles in muscle contraction and in a wide range of other&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#motile"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;motile">motility</span></a>&nbsp;processes in&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotes">eukaryotes</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="N" class="mw-headline">N</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="natural_selection" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Natural selection" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_selection">natural selection</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A process in nature in which organisms possessing certain&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#genotype"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;genotype">genotypic</span></a>&nbsp;characteristics that make them better adjusted to an environment tend to survive, reproduce, increase in number or&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gene frequency" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_frequency">frequency</a>, and therefore, are able to transmit and perpetuate their essential genotypic qualities to succeeding generations.</dd>
<dt id="neurobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Neurobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurobiology">neurobiology</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called&nbsp;<strong>neuroscience</strong>.</span></p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dd class="glossary">The scientific study of the&nbsp;<a title="Nervous system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nervous_system">nervous system</a>.</dd>
<dt id="neuron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Neuron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuron">neuron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An electrically excitable cell that receives, processes, and transmits information through electrical and chemical signals.</dd>
<dt id="neurotransmitter" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Neurotransmitter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurotransmitter">neurotransmitter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#endogenous"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;endogenous">endogenous</span></a>&nbsp;compound that enable&nbsp;<a title="Neurotransmission" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurotransmission">neurotransmission</a>.</dd>
<dt id="niche" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ecological niche" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_niche">niche</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The role and position an organism or taxon fills within its environment; how it meets its needs for food and shelter, how it survives, and how it reproduces. A species' niche includes all of its interactions with the biotic and abiotic factors of its environment.</dd>
<dt id="nucleic_acid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleic acid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleic_acid">nucleic acid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The biopolymers, or small&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Biomolecules" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomolecules">biomolecules</a>, essential to all known forms of life .</dd>
<dt id="nucleic_acid_sequence" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleic acid sequence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleic_acid_sequence">nucleic acid sequence</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A succession of letters that indicate the order of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotides" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotides">nucleotides</a>&nbsp;forming alleles within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;molecule.</dd>
<dt id="nucleobase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleobase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleobase">nucleobase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The nitrogen-containing biological compounds that form&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleosides" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleosides">nucleosides</a>, which in turn are components of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotides" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotides">nucleotides</a>, with all of these monomers constituting the basic building blocks of nucleic acids.</dd>
<dt id="nucleoid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleoid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleoid">nucleoid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An irregularly shaped region within the cell of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#prokaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;prokaryote">prokaryote</span></a>&nbsp;that contains all or most of the genetic material, called the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Genophore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genophore">genophore</a>.</dd>
<dt id="nucleolus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleolus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleolus">nucleolus</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The largest structure within the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleus">nucleus</span></a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#eukaryote"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;eukaryote">eukaryotic</span></a>&nbsp;cells.</dd>
<dt id="nucleotide" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Nucleotide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotide">nucleotide</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organic compound which serves as the fundamental&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#monomer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;monomer">monomer</span></a>&nbsp;used in the construction of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleic_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleic acid">nucleic acid</span></a>&nbsp;polymers, such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>, both of which are essential biomolecules within all living organisms.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="O" class="mw-headline">O</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="offspring" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Offspring" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Offspring">offspring</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="order" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Order (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_(biology)">order</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="organ" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Organ (anatomy)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)">organ</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A collection of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#tissue"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;tissue">tissues</span></a>&nbsp;joined in a structural unit to serve a common function.</dd>
<dt id="organism" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Organism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organism">organism</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A contiguous living system.</dd>
<dt id="ornithology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ornithology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ornithology">ornithology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of zoology that concerns the study of birds. Etymologically, the word "ornithology" derives from the ancient Greek &rho;&nu;&iota;&sigmaf;&nbsp;<em>ornis</em>&nbsp;("bird") and &lambda;&gamma;&omicron;&sigmaf;&nbsp;<em>logos</em>&nbsp;("rationale" or "explanation").</dd>
<dt id="osmosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Osmosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmosis">osmosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The spontaneous net movement of solvent molecules through a semipermeable membrane into a region of higher solute concentration, in the direction that tends to equalize the solute concentrations on the two sides.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="P" class="mw-headline">P</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="paleontology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Paleontology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleontology">paleontology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of the history of life on Earth as reflected in the fossil record. Fossils are the remains or traces of organisms (plants, animals, fungi, bacteria and other single-celled living things) that lived in the geological past and are preserved in the crust of the Earth.</dd>
<dt id="parallel_evolution" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Parallel evolution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_evolution">parallel evolution</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The development of a similar trait in related, but distinct, species descending from the same&nbsp;<a title="Ancestor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestor">ancestor</a>, but from different clades.</dd>
<dt id="parasite" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Parasite" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasite">parasite</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="parasitology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Parasitology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitology">parasitology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of parasites, their hosts, and the relationship between them. As a biological discipline, the scope of parasitology is not determined by the organism or environment in question, but by their way of life.</dd>
<dt id="pathobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Pathobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathobiology">pathobiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study or practice of pathology with greater emphasis on the biological than on the medical aspects.</dd>
<dt id="pathogen" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Pathogen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathogen">pathogen</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="pathology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Pathology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathology">pathology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A medical specialty that is concerned with the diagnosis of disease based on the laboratory analysis of bodily fluids such as blood and urine, as well as tissues, using the tools of chemistry, clinical microbiology, hematology and molecular pathology.</dd>
<dt id="ph" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="PH" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PH">pH</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A numeric scale used to specify the acidity or basicity (alkalinity) of an aqueous solution. It is roughly the negative of the logarithm to base 10 of the concentration, measured in units of moles per liter, of hydrogen ions.</dd>
<dt id="pharmacology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Pharmacology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmacology">pharmacology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The science of drug action on biological systems. In its entirety, it embraces knowledge of the sources, chemical properties, biological effects and therapeutic uses of drugs.</dd>
