<dt id="phenotype" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Phenotype" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenotype">phenotype</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The composite of an organism's observable features or traits, such as its morphology, development, biochemical or physiological properties, behavior, and products of behavior.</dd>
<dt id="pheromone" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Pheromone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pheromone">pheromone</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A secreted or excreted chemical factor that triggers a social response in members of the same&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="phloem" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Phloem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phloem">phloem</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The conducting tissue in plants responsible for the conduction of food particles.</dd>
<dt id="photosynthesis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Photosynthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="phylogeny" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Phylogeny" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylogeny">phylogeny</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="phylum" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Phylum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylum">phylum</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="physiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Physiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiology">physiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology dealing with the functions and activities of living organisms and their parts, including all physical and chemical processes.</dd>
<dt id="phytochemistry" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Phytochemistry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytochemistry">phytochemistry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Phytochemicals" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytochemicals">phytochemicals</a>, which are chemicals derived from plants.</dd>
<dt id="phytopathology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Phytopathology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytopathology">phytopathology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The science of diagnosing and managing plant diseases.</dd>
<dt id="placebo" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Placebo" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placebo">placebo</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a title="Chemical substance" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_substance">substance</a>&nbsp;or treatment of no intended therapeutic value.</dd>
<dt id="plant" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Plant" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant">plant</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="plasmolysis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Plasmolysis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmolysis">plasmolysis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process in which&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>&nbsp;lose water in a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertonic solution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertonic_solution">hypertonic solution</a>.</dd>
<dt id="pollination" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Pollination" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollination">pollination</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The transfer of&nbsp;<a title="Pollen" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollen">pollen</a>&nbsp;from a male part of a plant to a female part of a plant, enabling later fertilisation and the production of seeds, most often by an animal or by wind.</dd>
<dt id="polymer" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Polymer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymer">polymer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large&nbsp;<a title="Macromolecule" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macromolecule">macromolecule</a>&nbsp;composed of many repeated subunits.</dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="polymerase_chain_reaction_(pcr)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Polymerase chain reaction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymerase_chain_reaction">polymerase chain reaction</a>&nbsp;(PCR)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A technique used in&nbsp;<a title="Molecular biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_biology">molecular biology</a>&nbsp;to amplify a single copy or a few copies of a segment of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;across several orders of magnitude, generating thousands to millions of copies of a particular&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;sequence.</dd>
<dt id="polyploidy" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Polyploidy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyploidy">polyploidy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Having or containing more than two complete sets of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#chromosome"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;chromosome">chromosomes</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="population" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Population (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_(biology)">population</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="population_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Population biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_biology">population biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of populations of organisms, especially the regulation of population size, life history traits such as clutch size, and extinction.</dd>
<dt id="population_ecology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Population ecology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_ecology">population ecology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A subfield of ecology that deals with the dynamics of species populations and how these populations interact with the environment. It is the study of how the population sizes of species change over time and space. Also called&nbsp;<em>autoecology</em>.</dd>
<dt id="predation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Predation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predation">predation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A biological interaction in which a&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Predator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predator">predator</a>&nbsp;kills and eats its&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Prey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prey">prey</a>.</dd>
<dt id="predator" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Predator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predator">predator</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="prey" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Prey" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prey">prey</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="primase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Primase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primase">primase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a title="RNA polymerase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA_polymerase">RNA polymerase</a>&nbsp;involved in the replication of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="primer" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Primer (molecular biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primer_(molecular_biology)">primer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short strand of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;that serves as a starting point for&nbsp;<a title="DNA synthesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_synthesis">DNA synthesis</a>.</dd>
<dt id="progeny" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary">progeny</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any genetic descendant or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#offspring"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;offspring">offspring</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="progesterone" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Progesterone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progesterone">progesterone</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#endogenous"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;endogenous">endogenous</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#steroid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;steroid">steroid</span></a>&nbsp;and progestogen sex&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#hormone"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;hormone">hormone</span></a>&nbsp;which is part of the&nbsp;<a title="Menstrual cycle" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menstrual_cycle">menstrual cycle</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Pregnancy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Embryogenesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryogenesis">embryogenesis</a>&nbsp;of humans and other animal species.</dd>
<dt id="prokaryote" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Prokaryote" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryote">prokaryote</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An organism which does not have a true&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleus">nucleus</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="protein" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Protein" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protein">protein</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A polypeptide chain of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#amino_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;amino acid">amino acids</span></a>. It is a body-building nutrient.</dd>
<dt id="protein_structure" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Protein structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protein_structure">protein structure</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A three-dimensional arrangement of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Atoms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atoms">atoms</a>&nbsp;in an amino acid-chain molecule.</dd>
<dt id="protist" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Protist" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist">protist</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="psychobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Psychobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychobiology">psychobiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The application of the principles of biology to the study of physiological, genetic, and developmental mechanisms of behavior in humans and other animals. Also called&nbsp;<em>behavioral neuroscience</em>,&nbsp;<em>biological psychology</em>, and&nbsp;<em>biopsychology</em>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="R" class="mw-headline">R</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="regeneration" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Regeneration (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regeneration_(biology)">regeneration</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of renewal, restoration, and growth that makes genomes, cells, organisms, and ecosystems resilient to natural fluctuations or events that cause disturbance or damage.</dd>
<dt id="reproduction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reproduction">reproduction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Giving birth to one of its kind,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#sexual_reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;sexual reproduction">sexually</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#asexual_reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;asexual reproduction">asexually</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="reproductive_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Reproductive biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reproductive_biology">reproductive biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="ribonucleic_acid_(rna)" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Ribonucleic acid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ribonucleic_acid">ribonucleic acid</a>&nbsp;(RNA)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleic_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleic acid">nucleic acid</span></a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#polymer"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;polymer">polymer</span></a>&nbsp;composed of a series of&nbsp;<a title="Ribonucleotide" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ribonucleotide">ribonucleotides</a>&nbsp;which incorporate a set of four&nbsp;<a title="Nucleobase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleobase">nucleobases</a>:&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#adenine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;adenine">adenine</span></a>&nbsp;(A),&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#guanine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;guanine">guanine</span></a>&nbsp;(G),&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cytosine"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cytosine">cytosine</span></a>&nbsp;(C), and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#uracil"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;uracil">uracil</span></a>&nbsp;(U). Closely related to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>, RNA molecules serve in a wide variety of essential biological roles, including&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#genetic_code"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;genetic code">coding</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#translation"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;translation">decoding</span></a>, regulating, and expressing&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#gene"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;gene">genes</span></a>, as well as functioning as signaling molecules.</dd>
<dt id="ribosome" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ribosome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ribosome">ribosome</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A complex molecular machine, found within all living&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>, that serves as the site of biological protein synthesis.</dd>
<dt id="rna" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="RNA" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA">RNA</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">ribonucleic acid</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="rna_polymerase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="RNA polymerase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA_polymerase">RNA polymerase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A member of a family of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Enzymes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzymes">enzymes</a>&nbsp;that are essential to life: they are found in all organisms and many&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Viruses" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viruses">viruses</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="S" class="mw-headline">S</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="sclerenchyma" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Ground tissue" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ground_tissue#Sclerenchyma">sclerenchyma</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#tissue"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;tissue">tissue</span></a>&nbsp;in which cells have thick lignified secondary walls and often die when mature.</dd>
<dt id="seed" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Seed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seed">seed</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>, enclosed in a protective outer covering, of certain types of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#plant"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;plant">plants</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="selective_breeding" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Selective breeding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selective_breeding">selective breeding</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#artificial_selection"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;artificial selection">artificial selection</span></a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="sessile" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sessility (motility)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sessility_(motility)">sessile</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="sex" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sex" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex">sex</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="sexual_reproduction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sexual reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_reproduction">sexual reproduction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#reproduction"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;reproduction">reproduction</span></a>&nbsp;in which&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cells</span></a>&nbsp;from two parents unite to form the first cell of a new organism.</dd>
<dt id="sociality" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sociality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociality">sociality</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The degree to which individuals in an&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#animal"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;animal">animal</span></a>&nbsp;population tend to associate in social groups and form cooperative societies.</dd>
<dt id="sociobiology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sociobiology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociobiology">sociobiology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A field of scientific study that is based on the hypothesis that social behavior has resulted from evolution and attempts to explain and examine social behavior within that context.</dd>
<dt id="soil_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Soil biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil_biology">soil biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The study of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Microbial" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microbial">microbial</a>&nbsp;and faunal activity and ecology in&nbsp;<a title="Soil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil">soil</a>.</dd>
<dt id="species" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Species" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species">species</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The basic unit of classification and a&nbsp;<a title="Taxonomy (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)">taxonomic</a>&nbsp;rank, as well as a unit of biodiversity, but it has proven difficult to find a satisfactory definition.</dd>
<dt id="speciation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Speciation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speciation">speciation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The evolutionary process by which populations evolve to become distinct&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="sperm" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Sperm" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sperm">sperm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="spore" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Spore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spore">spore</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="stem_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Stem cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stem_cell">stem cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The biological cells that can differentiate into other types of cells and can divide to produce more of the same type of stem cells.</dd>
<dt id="steroid" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Steroid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steroid">steroid</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A biologically active organic compound with four rings arranged in a specific molecular configuration.</dd>
<dt id="strain" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Strain (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strain_(biology)">strain</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="structural_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Structural biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Structural_biology">structural biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#molecular_biology"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;molecular biology">molecular biology</span></a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#biochemistry"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;biochemistry">biochemistry</span></a>, and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#biophysics"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;biophysics">biophysics</span></a>&nbsp;concerned with the molecular structure of biological&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#macromolecule"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;macromolecule">macromolecules</span></a>, especially&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#protein"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;protein">proteins</span></a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleic_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleic acid">nucleic acids</span></a>, how they acquire the structures they have, and how alterations in their structures affect their function.</dd>
<dt id="symbiogenesis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Symbiogenesis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbiogenesis">symbiogenesis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An evolutionary theory of the origin of eukaryotic cells from prokaryotic organisms occurring from symbiosis.</dd>
<dt id="symbiont" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Symbiont" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbiont">symbiont</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="symbiosis" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Symbiosis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbiosis">symbiosis</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any close and long-term biological interaction between two different biological organisms, regardless of the nature or degree of the effect on either organism. Examples include&nbsp;<a title="Mutualism (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutualism_(biology)">mutualism</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Commensalism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commensalism">commensalism</a>, and&nbsp;<a title="Parasitism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitism">parasitism</a>.</dd>
<dt id="synthetic_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Synthetic biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synthetic_biology">synthetic biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An interdisciplinary branch of biology and engineering. The subject combines various disciplines from within these domains, such as biotechnology, evolutionary biology, molecular biology, systems biology, biophysics, computer engineering, and genetic engineering.</dd>
<dt id="systematics" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Systematics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systematics">systematics</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The scientific study of biodiversity. It is concerned with the discovering and naming of new species of organisms (nomenclature) and arranging these taxa into classification schemes (taxonomy). A large part of modern systematics concerns establishing the evolutionary relationships among various taxa (phylogenetics) using methods of comparative biology (e.g. physiology, behavior, biochemistry, morphology, genetics) and statistical analysis.</dd>
<dt id="systems_biology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Systems biology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systems_biology">systems biology</a></dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<h2><span id="T" class="mw-headline">T</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="t_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="T cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T_cell">T cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of&nbsp;<a title="Lymphocyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lymphocyte">lymphocyte</a>&nbsp;that plays a central role in cell-mediated&nbsp;<a title="Immunity (medical)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunity_(medical)">immunity</a>.</dd>
<dt id="taxon" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Taxon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxon">taxon</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of one or more populations of an organism or organisms seen by&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Taxonomists" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomists">taxonomists</a>&nbsp;to form a unit.</dd>
<dt id="taxonomy" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Taxonomy (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)">taxonomy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="telophase" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Telophase" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telophase">telophase</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="testosterone" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Testosterone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testosterone">testosterone</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The primary male sex hormone and an anabolic&nbsp;<a title="Steroid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steroid">steroid</a>.</dd>
<dt id="thymine" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Thymine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thymine">thymine</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the four&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleobases" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleobases">nucleobases</a>&nbsp;in the nucleic acid of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;that are represented by the letters G&ndash;C&ndash;A&ndash;T.</dd>
<dt id="tissue" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Tissue (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tissue_(biology)">tissue</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="trait" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Phenotypic trait" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenotypic_trait">trait</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="transcription" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Transcription (genetics)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcription_(genetics)">transcription</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Transcription is the first step of gene expression, in which a particular segment of DNA is copied into RNA (mRNA) by the enzyme RNA polymerase. Both RNA and DNA are nucleic acids, which use base pairs of nucleotides as a complementary language.</dd>
<dt id="translation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Translation (biology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translation_(biology)">translation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process in which&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ribosomes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ribosomes">ribosomes</a>&nbsp;in the cytoplasm or ER synthesize proteins after the process of transcription of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;in the cell's nucleus.</dd>
<dt id="trophic_level" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Trophic level" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_level">trophic level</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The position an organism occupies in a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#food_chain"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;food chain">food chain</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="tumor" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Tumor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tumor">tumor</a></dfn></dt>
</dl>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also called a&nbsp;<strong>neoplasm</strong>.</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote">&nbsp;</p>
<h2><span id="U" class="mw-headline">U</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="unicellular" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Unicellular organism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicellular_organism">unicellular</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Having or consisting of only one&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>, as opposed to being&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#multicellular"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;multicellular">multicellular</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="uracil" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Uracil" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uracil">uracil</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the four nucleobases in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#nucleic_acid"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;nucleic acid">nucleic acid</span></a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;that are represented by the letters A, G, C and U.</dd>
<dt id="urea" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Urea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urea">urea</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An&nbsp;<a title="Organic compound" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_compound">organic</a>&nbsp;compound with chemical formula CO(NH<sub>2</sub>)<sub>2</sub>.</dd>
<dt id="urine" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Urine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urine">urine</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A liquid byproduct of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#metabolism"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;metabolism">metabolism</span></a>&nbsp;in humans and in many animals.</dd>
<dt id="uterus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Uterus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uterus">uterus</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A major female hormone-responsive secondary sex organ of the&nbsp;<a title="Reproductive system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reproductive_system">reproductive system</a>&nbsp;in humans and most other&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammals">mammals</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="V" class="mw-headline">V</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="vacuole" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vacuole" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuole">vacuole</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A membrane-bound organelle which is present in all plant and fungal cells and some protist, animal and bacterial cells.</dd>
<dt id="valence_electron" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Valence electron" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valence_electron">valence electron</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valence electron is an electron that is associated with an atom, and that can participate in the formation of a chemical bond; in a single covalent bond, both atoms in the bond contribute one valence electron in order to form a shared pair.</dd>
<dt id="vasodilation" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vasodilation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vasodilation">vasodilation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The widening of blood vessels.</dd>
<dt id="vector" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vector (epidemiology)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vector_(epidemiology)">vector</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="vegetative_reproduction" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vegetative reproduction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetative_reproduction">vegetative reproduction</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The type of reproduction in which sexual process is not involved, also known as asexual reproduction.</dd>
<dt id="vertebrate" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vertebrate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertebrate">vertebrate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
<dt id="vesicle" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vesicle (biology and chemistry)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesicle_(biology_and_chemistry)">vesicle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small structure within a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#cell"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;cell">cell</span></a>, or&nbsp;<a title="Extracellular" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extracellular">extracellular</a>, consisting of fluid enclosed by a lipid&nbsp;<a title="Bilayer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bilayer">bilayer</a>.</dd>
<dt id="vestigiality" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Vestigiality" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vestigiality">vestigiality</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The retention during the process of evolution of genetically determined structures or attributes that have lost some or all of their ancestral function in a given&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#species"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;species">species</span></a>.</dd>
<dt id="virology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Virology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virology">virology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#virus"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;virus">viruses</span></a></dd>
<dt id="virus" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Virus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virus">virus</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A submicroscopic, infectious, parasitic particle of genetic material contained in a protein coat and which replicates only inside the living cell of a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#host"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;host">host</span></a>&nbsp;organism.</dd>
<dd class="glossary"></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="W" class="mw-headline">W</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="white_blood_cell" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="White blood cell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_blood_cell">white blood cell</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Leukocyte" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leukocyte">leukocyte</a></em>.</dd>
<dt id="whole_genome_sequencing" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Whole genome sequencing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whole_genome_sequencing">whole genome sequencing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of determining the complete&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#dNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;DNA">DNA</span></a>&nbsp;sequence of an organism's genome at a single time.</dd>
<dt id="wobble_base_pair" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Wobble base pair" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wobble_base_pair">wobble base pair</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pairing between two nucleotides in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#rNA"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;RNA">RNA</span></a>&nbsp;molecules that does not follow Watson-Crick base pair rules.</dd>
<dt id="wood" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Wood" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wood">wood</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The inner layer of the stems of woody plants, composed of&nbsp;<a title="Xylem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xylem">xylem</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="X" class="mw-headline">X</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="xanthophyll" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Xanthophyll" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xanthophyll">xanthophyll</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The yellow colored photosynthetic pigments.</dd>
<dt id="xylem" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Xylem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xylem">xylem</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The plant tissue responsible for the conduction of water from roots to aerial parts of the plant. It forms the woody part of the plant.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Y" class="mw-headline">Y</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="yolk" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Yolk" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yolk">yolk</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The nutrient-bearing portion of the egg whose primary function is to supply food for the development of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#embryo"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;embryo">embryo</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span id="Z" class="mw-headline">Z</span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt id="zoology" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Zoology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoology">zoology</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The branch of biology that studies the animal kingdom, including the&nbsp;<a title="Structure" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Structure">structure</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Embryology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryology">embryology</a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_biology#evolution"><span id="" class="glossary-link-internal" title="See entry on this page at &sect;evolution">evolution</span></a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific classification" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_classification">classification</a>,&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Habits" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habits">habits</a>, and distribution of all animals, both living and extinct, and how they interact with their&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystems">ecosystems</a>.</dd>
<dt id="zooplankton" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Zooplankton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zooplankton">zooplankton</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Are&nbsp;<a title="Heterotroph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotroph">heterotrophic</a>&nbsp;(sometimes&nbsp;<a title="Detritivore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detritivore">detritivorous</a>)&nbsp;<a title="Plankton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plankton">plankton</a>&nbsp;(cf.&nbsp;<a title="Phytoplankton" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytoplankton">phytoplankton</a>). Plankton are organisms drifting in&nbsp;<a title="Ocean" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean">oceans</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Sea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea">seas</a>, and bodies of&nbsp;<a title="Fresh water" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fresh_water">fresh water</a>. Individual zooplankton are usually&nbsp;<a title="Microscopic scale" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microscopic_scale">microscopic</a>, but some (such as&nbsp;<a title="Jellyfish" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jellyfish">jellyfish</a>) are larger and&nbsp;<a title="Macroscopic scale" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macroscopic_scale">visible</a>&nbsp;to the&nbsp;<a title="Naked eye" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naked_eye">naked eye</a>.</dd>
<dt id="zygospore" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Zygospore" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zygospore">zygospore</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Diploid" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diploid">diploid</a>&nbsp;reproductive stage in the life cycle of many&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi">fungi</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Protists" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protists">protists</a>.</dd>
<dt id="zygote" class="glossary"><dfn class="glossary"><a title="Zygote" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zygote">zygote</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic">eukaryotic</a>&nbsp;cell formed by a fertilization event between two&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Gametes" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gametes">gametes</a>.</dd>
</dl>




</br>
